## what's up?; what's wrong?
### zÄ›nme le
---
- **definition:** what's up?; what's wrong?
- **pinyin:** zÄ›nme le
- **components:**
  - æ€
    - zÄ›n
    - how; why
  - ä¹ˆ(éº¼)
    - me
    - suffix for forming questions or adverbs of manner
  - äº†
    - le
    - particle indicating change, completion, or new situation
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** æ€(æ€) (zÄ›n, "how; why") + éº¼(éº¼) (me, "suffix for forming questions or adverbs of manner") + äº†(äº†) (le, "particle indicating change, completion, or new situation")
  - **interpretation:** The phrase æ€éº¼äº†(æ€ä¹ˆäº†) (zÄ›nme le) combines æ€(æ€) (zÄ›n, "how") with the interrogative suffix éº¼(éº¼) (me), and the particle äº†(äº†) (le), which indicates a change or new situation. It is used to inquire about someone's condition or situation, like asking "what's up?" or "what's wrong?" in English. The use of äº†(äº†) (le) suggests that the speaker is referring to a situation that has changed or developed.
- **examples:**
  - ä½ æ€ä¹ˆäº†(ä½ æ€éº¼äº†)ï¼Ÿ
    - NÇ zÄ›nme le?
    - What's wrong with you?
  - ä½ çœ‹èµ·æ¥ä¸å¤ªèˆ’æœ(ä½ çœ‹èµ·ä¾†ä¸å¤ªèˆ’æœ)ï¼Œæ€ä¹ˆäº†(æ€éº¼äº†)ï¼Ÿ
    - NÇ kÃ n qÇlÃ¡i bÃ¹ tÃ i shÅ«fu, zÄ›nme le?

### dÄ›ngdÄ›ng

  - **description:** ç­‰(ç­‰) (dÄ›ng, "wait; rank; class") + ç­‰(ç­‰) (dÄ›ng, "wait; rank; class") is a repetition used to indicate continuation, often translated as "etc." or "and so on." This suggests incompleteness, indicating that what has been mentioned is part of a larger list or sequence.

## å¤©å•Š(å¤©å•Š)
---
## oh my god
### tiÄn a
---
- **definition:** oh my god
- **pinyin:** tiÄn a
- **components:**
  - å¤©
    - tiÄn
    - heaven; sky
  - å•Š
    - a
    - a modal particle expressing surprise or exclamation
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** å¤©(å¤©) (tiÄn, "heaven; sky") + å•Š(å•Š) (a, "a modal particle expressing surprise or exclamation")
  - **interpretation:** The phrase å¤©å•Š (tiÄn a) expresses surprise, shock, or amazement. The character å¤©(å¤©) (tiÄn, "heaven; sky") invokes a greater power or the heavens, while the particle å•Š(å•Š) (a, "a modal particle") emphasizes the emotional reaction. Together, this expression is akin to saying 'oh my god' in English.
- **examples:**
  - å¤©å•Š(å¤©å•Š)ï¼

## å¥½çš„(å¥½çš„)
---
## ok; all right
### hÇo de
---
- **definition:** ok; all right
- **pinyin:** hÇo de
- **components:**
  - å¥½
    - hÇo
    - good; fine; well
  - çš„
    - de
    - particle used for emphasis or possession
- **etymology:**
  - **type:** compound word
  - **description:** å¥½(å¥½) (hÇo, "good") + çš„(çš„) (de, "particle used for emphasis or possession")
  - **interpretation:** å¥½çš„ (hÇo de) is used to indicate agreement or affirmation, similarly to saying 'okay' or 'alright' in English. The character å¥½(å¥½) (hÇo, "good") conveys a positive response, while çš„(çš„) (de) is a particle that adds emphasis, making the phrase a polite and affirmative reply.
- **examples:**
  - æˆ‘ä»¬æ˜å¤©è§(æˆ‘å€‘æ˜å¤©è¦‹)ï¼Œå¥½çš„(å¥½çš„)ã€‚
    - wÇ’men mÃ­ngtiÄn jiÃ n, hÇo de.
    - We will meet tomorrow, alright.
  - å¬åˆ°æ¶ˆæ¯å(è½åˆ°æ¶ˆæ¯å¾Œ)ï¼Œæˆ‘è¯´å¥½çš„(æˆ‘èªªå¥½çš„)ã€‚
